<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_members">Former members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Former members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_China">Republic of China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Republic of China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/China_and_the_United_Nations" title="China and the United Nations">China and the United Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:China_map.png" class="image"><img alt="A map of East Asia highlighting the Chinese states" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/China_map.png/220px-China_map.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/China_map.png/330px-China_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/China_map.png/440px-China_map.png 2x" data-file-width="705" data-file-height="705" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:China_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Areas controlled by the People's Republic of China and the Republic of China</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">Republic of China</a> (ROC) joined the UN as an original member on 24 October 1945, and as set out by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" title="United Nations Charter">United Nations Charter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chapter_V_of_the_United_Nations_Charter" title="Chapter V of the United Nations Charter">Chapter V</a>, Article 23, became one of the five permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-charter_ch5_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter_ch5-46">[18]</a></sup> In 1949, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a>-led ROC government lost effective control of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">mainland China</a> and relocated to the <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Taiwan" class="mw-redirect" title="Island of Taiwan">island of Taiwan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party</a>-led government of the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> (PRC), declared on 1 October 1949, took control of mainland China. The UN was notified on 18 November 1949 of the formation of the <a href="/wiki/State_Council_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="State Council of the People's Republic of China">Central People's Government of the People's Republic of China</a>; however, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Government of the Republic of China">Government of the Republic of China</a> continued to represent China at the UN, despite the small size of the ROC's jurisdiction of <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="List of islands of the Republic of China">Taiwan and a number of smaller islands</a> compared to the PRC's jurisdiction of mainland China. As both governments claimed to be the sole legitimate representative of China, proposals to effect a change in the representation of China in the UN were discussed but rejected for the next two decades, as the ROC was still recognized as the sole legitimate representative of China by a majority of UN members.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Both sides rejected compromise proposals to allow both states to participate in the UN, based on the <a href="/wiki/One-China_policy" title="One-China policy">One-China policy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the 1970s, a shift had occurred in international diplomatic circles and the PRC had gained the upper hand in international diplomatic relations and recognition count. On 25 October 1971, the 21st time the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> debated on the PRC's admission into the UN,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_2758" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758">United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758</a> was adopted, by which it recognized that "the representatives of the Government of the People's Republic of China are the only lawful representatives of China to the United Nations and that the People's Republic of China is one of the five permanent members of the Security Council," and decided "to restore all its rights to the People's Republic of China and to recognize the representatives of its Government as the only legitimate representatives of China to the United Nations, and to expel forthwith the representatives of <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a> from the place which they unlawfully occupy at the United Nations and in all the organizations related to it."<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[21]</a></sup> This effectively transferred the seat of China in the UN, including its permanent seat on the Security Council, from the ROC to the PRC, and expelled the ROC from the UN. From the United Nations' perspective the "Republic of China" is not a former member. No UN member was expelled in 1971. Rather, the credentials of one Chinese delegation (from Taipei) were rejected and the credentials of another Chinese delegation (from Beijing) were accepted.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In addition to losing its seat in the UN, the UN Secretary-General concluded from the resolution that the General Assembly considered Taiwan to be a province of China. Consequently, the Secretary-General decided that it was not permitted for the ROC to become a party to treaties deposited with it.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bids_for_readmission_as_the_representative_of_Taiwan">Bids for readmission as the representative of Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Bids for readmission as the representative of Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">Political status of Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Four-Stage_Theory_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Four-Stage Theory of the Republic of China">Four-Stage Theory of the Republic of China</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Voa_chinese_ma_ying_jeou_tw_09Oct10_480.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ma Ying-jeou stands behind a podium decked with flowers" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Voa_chinese_ma_ying_jeou_tw_09Oct10_480.jpg/220px-Voa_chinese_ma_ying_jeou_tw_09Oct10_480.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Voa_chinese_ma_ying_jeou_tw_09Oct10_480.jpg/330px-Voa_chinese_ma_ying_jeou_tw_09Oct10_480.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Voa_chinese_ma_ying_jeou_tw_09Oct10_480.jpg/440px-Voa_chinese_ma_ying_jeou_tw_09Oct10_480.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="350" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Voa_chinese_ma_ying_jeou_tw_09Oct10_480.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The presidency of <a href="/wiki/Ma_Ying-jeou" title="Ma Ying-jeou">Ma Ying-jeou</a> saw the first participation of the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> on a United Nations body in almost 40 years.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1993 the ROC began campaigning to rejoin the UN separately from the People's Republic of China. A number of options were considered, including seeking membership in the <a href="/wiki/Specialized_agencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Specialized agencies">specialized agencies</a>, applying for <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">observer status</a>, applying for full membership, or having resolution 2758 revoked to reclaim the seat of China in the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindemann_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindemann-51">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Every year from 1993–2006, UN member states submitted a memorandum to the UN Secretary-General requesting that the UN General Assembly consider allowing the ROC to resume participating in the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[24]</a></sup> This approach was chosen, rather than a formal application for membership, because it could be enacted by the General Assembly, while a membership application would need Security Council approval, where the PRC held a veto.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindemann_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindemann-51">[23]</a></sup> Early proposals recommended admitting the ROC with parallel representation over China, along with the People's Republic of China, pending eventual reunification, citing examples of other divided countries which had become separate UN member states, such as <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>. Later proposals emphasized that the ROC was a separate state, over which the PRC had no effective sovereignty. These proposed resolutions referred to the ROC under a variety of names: "Republic of China in Taiwan" (1993–94), "Republic of China on Taiwan" (1995–97, 1999–2002), "Republic of China" (1998), "Republic of China (Taiwan)" (2003) and "Taiwan" (2004–06).</p>
<p>However, all fourteen attempts were unsuccessful as the General Assembly's General Committee declined to put the issue on the Assembly's agenda for debate, under strong opposition from the PRC.<sup id="cite_ref-europers_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europers-53">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>While all these proposals were vague, requesting the ROC be allowed to participate in UN activities without specifying any legal mechanism, in 2007 the ROC submitted a formal application under the name "Taiwan" for full membership in the UN.<sup id="cite_ref-A.2F62.2F193_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A.2F62.2F193-54">[26]</a></sup> However, the application was rejected by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_of_Legal_Affairs" title="United Nations Office of Legal Affairs">United Nations Office of Legal Affairs</a> citing General Assembly Resolution 2758,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[27]</a></sup> without being forwarded to the Security Council. <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> stated that:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The position of the United Nations is that the People's Republic of China is representing the whole of China as the sole and legitimate representative Government of China. The decision until now about the wish of the people in Taiwan to join the United Nations has been decided on that basis. The resolution (General Assembly Resolution 2758) that you just mentioned is clearly mentioning that the Government of China is the sole and legitimate Government and the position of the United Nations is that Taiwan is part of China.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[28]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Responding to the UN's rejection of its application, the ROC government has stated that Taiwan is not now nor has it ever been under the jurisdiction of the PRC, and that since General Assembly Resolution 2758 did not clarify the issue of Taiwan's representation in the UN, it does not prevent Taiwan's participation in the UN as an independent sovereign nation.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[29]</a></sup> The ROC government also criticized Ban for asserting that Taiwan is part of China and returning the application without passing it to the Security Council or the General Assembly,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[30]</a></sup> contrary to UN's standard procedure (Provisional Rules of Procedure of the Security Council, Chapter X, Rule 59).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[31]</a></sup> On the other hand, the PRC government, which has stated that Taiwan is part of China and firmly opposes the application of any Taiwan authorities to join the UN either as a member or an observer, praised that UN's decision "was made in accordance with the UN Charter and Resolution 2758 of the UN General Assembly, and showed the UN and its member states' universal adherence to the <a href="/wiki/One-China_policy" title="One-China policy">one-China principle</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[32]</a></sup> A group of UN member states put forward a draft resolution for that fall's UN General Assembly calling on the Security Council to consider the application.<sup id="cite_ref-A.2F62.2F193_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A.2F62.2F193-54">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following year <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_United_Nations_membership_referendums,_2008" title="Taiwanese United Nations membership referendums, 2008">two referendums</a> in Taiwan on the government's attempts to regain participation at the UN did not pass due to low turnout. That fall the ROC took a new approach, with its allies submitting a resolution requesting that the "Republic of China (Taiwan)" be allowed to have "meaningful participation" in the UN <a href="/wiki/Specialized_agencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Specialized agencies">specialized agencies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[33]</a></sup> Again the issue was not put on the Assembly's agenda.<sup id="cite_ref-europers_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europers-53">[25]</a></sup> In 2009, the ROC chose not to bring the issue of its participation in the UN up for debate at the General Assembly for the first time since it began the campaign in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health_(Republic_of_China)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Health (Republic of China)">Department of Health of the Republic of China</a> was invited by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> to attend the 62nd <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Assembly" title="World Health Assembly">World Health Assembly</a> as an observer under the name "<a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei" title="Chinese Taipei">Chinese Taipei</a>". This was the ROC's first participation in an event organized by a <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">UN-affiliated agency</a> since 1971, as a result of the improved <a href="/wiki/Cross-strait_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Cross-strait relations">cross-strait relations</a> since <a href="/wiki/Ma_Ying-jeou" title="Ma Ying-jeou">Ma Ying-jeou</a> became the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">President of the Republic of China</a> a year before.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Republic of China is officially <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="International recognition of the Republic of China">recognized by&#160;20&#160;UN member states</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>. It maintains unofficial diplomatic relations with many other nations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Czechoslovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> joined the UN as an original member on 24 October 1945, with its name changed to the Czech and Slovak Federative Republic on 20 April 1990. Upon the imminent <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">dissolution of Czechoslovakia</a>, in a letter dated 10 December 1992, its Permanent Representative informed the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">United Nations Secretary-General</a> that the Czech and Slovak Federative Republic would cease to exist on 31 December 1992 and that the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, as successor states, would apply for membership in the UN. Neither state sought sole successor state status. Both states were admitted to the UN on 19 January 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German_Democratic_Republic">German Democratic Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: German Democratic Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Both the <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">Federal Republic of Germany</a> (West Germany) and the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">German Democratic Republic</a> (East Germany) were admitted to the UN on 18 September 1973. Through the <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">accession of the East German federal states to the Federal Republic of Germany</a>, effective from 3 October 1990, the territory of the German Democratic Republic became part of the Federal Republic of Germany, today simply known as <i>Germany</i>. Consequently, the Federal Republic of Germany continued being a member of the UN while the German Democratic Republic ceased to exist.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federation_of_Malaya">Federation of Malaya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Federation of Malaya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Federation of Malaya</a> joined the United Nations on 17 September 1957. On 16 September 1963, its name was changed to <b><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a></b>, following the formation of Malaysia from <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_North_Borneo" title="Crown Colony of North Borneo">North Borneo</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a>), <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Sarawak" title="Crown Colony of Sarawak">Sarawak</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya" title="Federation of Malaya">Federation of Malaya</a>. Singapore became an independent State on 9 August 1965 and a Member of the United Nations on 21 September 1965.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tanganyika_and_Zanzibar">Tanganyika and Zanzibar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tanganyika and Zanzibar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tanganyika" title="Tanganyika">Tanganyika</a> was admitted to the UN on 14 December 1961, and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Zanzibar_and_Pemba" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of Zanzibar and Pemba">Zanzibar</a> was admitted to the UN on 16 December 1963. Following the ratification on 26 April 1964 of the Articles of Union between Tanganyika and Zanzibar, the two states merged to form the single member "United Republic of Tanganyika and Zanzibar", with its name changed to the <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">United Republic of Tanzania</a> on 1 November 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics">Union of Soviet Socialist Republics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Union of Soviet Socialist Republics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_and_the_United_Nations" title="Soviet Union and the United Nations">Soviet Union and the United Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soviet_Union_map_1945-09-20_to_1946-02-02.png" class="image"><img alt="A map of Eurasia highlighting the USSR" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Soviet_Union_map_1945-09-20_to_1946-02-02.png/220px-Soviet_Union_map_1945-09-20_to_1946-02-02.png" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Soviet_Union_map_1945-09-20_to_1946-02-02.png/330px-Soviet_Union_map_1945-09-20_to_1946-02-02.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Soviet_Union_map_1945-09-20_to_1946-02-02.png/440px-Soviet_Union_map_1945-09-20_to_1946-02-02.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1210" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soviet_Union_map_1945-09-20_to_1946-02-02.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The USSR as its borders and republics were configured upon entry to the UN. Border changes and the dissolution of various republics happened over the course of its membership.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Union of Soviet Socialist Republics</a> (USSR) joined the UN as an original member on 24 October 1945, and as set out by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" title="United Nations Charter">United Nations Charter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chapter_V_of_the_United_Nations_Charter" title="Chapter V of the United Nations Charter">Chapter V</a>, Article 23, became one of the five permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-charter_ch5_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter_ch5-46">[18]</a></sup> Upon the imminent <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union_(1982%E2%80%931991)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Soviet Union (1982–1991)">dissolution of the USSR</a>, in a letter dated 24 December 1991, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">President of the Russian Federation</a>, informed the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">United Nations Secretary-General</a> that the membership of the USSR in the Security Council and all other UN organs was being continued by the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian Federation</a> with the support of the 11 member countries of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The other fourteen independent states established from the former Soviet Republics were all admitted to the UN:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> joined the UN on 24 October 1945 together with the USSR. After declaring independence, the Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic changed its name to <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> on 24 August 1991, and on 19 September 1991, the Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic informed the UN that it had changed its name to <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> were admitted to the UN on 17 September 1991, after <a href="/wiki/State_continuity_of_the_Baltic_states" title="State continuity of the Baltic states">regaining independence</a> before the dissolution of the USSR.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Republic of Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> were admitted to the UN on 2 March 1992.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> was admitted to the UN on 31 July 1992.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Arab_Republic">United Arab Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: United Arab Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NasserQuwatliUAR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/NasserQuwatliUAR.jpg/220px-NasserQuwatliUAR.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/NasserQuwatliUAR.jpg/330px-NasserQuwatliUAR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/NasserQuwatliUAR.jpg/440px-NasserQuwatliUAR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="433" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NasserQuwatliUAR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Egyptian president <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a> (seated right) and Syrian president <a href="/wiki/Shukri_al-Quwatli" title="Shukri al-Quwatli">Shukri al-Quwatli</a> sign the accord to form the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Republic" title="United Arab Republic">United Arab Republic</a> in 1958. The short-lived political union briefly represented both states and was used as the name of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> following <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>'s withdrawal in 1961.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Both <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> joined the UN as original members on 24 October 1945. Following a plebiscite on 21 February 1958, the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Republic" title="United Arab Republic">United Arab Republic</a> was established by a union of Egypt and Syria and continued as a single member. On 13 October 1961, Syria, having resumed its status as an independent state, resumed its separate membership in the UN. Egypt continued as a UN member under the name of the United Arab Republic, until it reverted to its original name on 2 September 1971. Syria changed its name to the Syrian Arab Republic on 14 September 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yemen_and_Democratic_Yemen">Yemen and Democratic Yemen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Yemen and Democratic Yemen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/North_Yemen" title="North Yemen">Yemen</a> (i.e., North Yemen) was admitted to the UN on 30 September 1947; <a href="/wiki/South_Yemen" title="South Yemen">Southern Yemen</a> (i.e., South Yemen) was admitted to the UN on 14 December 1967, with its name changed to the People's Democratic Republic of Yemen on 30 November 1970, and was later referred to as Democratic Yemen. On 22 May 1990, <a href="/wiki/Yemeni_unification" title="Yemeni unification">the two states merged</a> to form the Republic of Yemen, which continued as a single member under the name <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Yugoslavia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_Yugoslavia_2006.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Former_Yugoslavia_2006.svg/220px-Former_Yugoslavia_2006.svg.png" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Former_Yugoslavia_2006.svg/330px-Former_Yugoslavia_2006.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Former_Yugoslavia_2006.svg/440px-Former_Yugoslavia_2006.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1832" data-file-height="1142" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_Yugoslavia_2006.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> disintegrated into several states starting in the early 1990s. By 2006, six UN member states existed in its former territory. Kosovo declared independence in 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>, referred to as Yugoslavia, joined the UN as an original member on 24 October 1945. By 1992, it had been effectively <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">dissolved</a> into five independent states, which were all subsequently admitted to the UN:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> were admitted to the UN on 22 May 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> was admitted to the UN on 8 April 1993, being provisionally referred to for all purposes within the UN as "The former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia" pending settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_naming_dispute" title="Macedonia naming dispute">difference that had arisen over its name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> (name later changed to Serbia and Montenegro) was admitted to the UN on 1 November 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-fr_yugoslavia_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fr_yugoslavia-68">[40]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Due to the dispute over its legal <a href="/wiki/Succession_of_states" title="Succession of states">successor states</a>, the member state "Yugoslavia", referring to the former Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia, remained on the official roster of UN members for many years after its effective dissolution.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup> Following the admission of all five states as new UN members, "Yugoslavia" was removed from the official roster of UN members.</p>
<p>The government of the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia, established on 28 April 1992 by the remaining Yugoslav republics of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Montenegro_(1992%E2%80%932006)" title="Republic of Montenegro (1992–2006)">Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Serbia_(1990%E2%80%932006)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Serbia (1990–2006)">Serbia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-nytfry_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytfry-69">[41]</a></sup> claimed itself as the legal <a href="/wiki/Succession_of_states" title="Succession of states">successor state</a> of the former Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia;<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[42]</a></sup> however, on 30 May 1992, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_757" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 757">United Nations Security Council Resolution 757</a> was adopted, by which it imposed <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions" title="International sanctions">international sanctions</a> on the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia due to its role in the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a>, and noted that "the claim by the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia (Serbia and Montenegro) to continue automatically the membership of the former Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia in the United Nations has not been generally accepted,"<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[43]</a></sup> and on 22 September 1992, United Nations General Assembly Resolution A/RES/47/1 was adopted, by which it considered that "the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia (Serbia and Montenegro) cannot continue automatically the membership of the former Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia in the United Nations," and therefore decided that "the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia (Serbia and Montenegro) should apply for membership in the United Nations and that it shall not participate in the work of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[45]</a></sup> The Federal Republic of Yugoslavia refused to comply with the resolution for many years, but following the ousting of <a href="/wiki/President_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="President of Serbia and Montenegro">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a> from office, it applied for membership, and was admitted to the UN on 1 November 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-fr_yugoslavia_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fr_yugoslavia-68">[40]</a></sup> On 4 February 2003, the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia had its official name changed to Serbia and Montenegro, following the adoption and promulgation of the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Charter_of_Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Constitutional Charter of Serbia and Montenegro">Constitutional Charter of Serbia and Montenegro</a> by the Assembly of the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the basis of a <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_independence_referendum,_2006" title="Montenegrin independence referendum, 2006">referendum</a> held on 21 May 2006, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> declared independence from <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Serbia and Montenegro</a> on 3 June 2006. In a letter dated on the same day, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Serbia" title="President of Serbia">President of Serbia</a> informed the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">United Nations Secretary-General</a> that the membership of Serbia and Montenegro in the UN was being continued by <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, following Montenegro's declaration of independence, in accordance with the Constitutional Charter of Serbia and Montenegro.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[47]</a></sup> Montenegro was admitted to the UN on 28 June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a>, the territory of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, then an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">autonomous province</a> of the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia, was put under the interim administration of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Administration_Mission_in_Kosovo" title="United Nations Interim Administration Mission in Kosovo">United Nations Mission in Kosovo</a> on 10 June 1999. On 17 February 2008 it declared independence, but this has not been recognised by Serbia. The <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> is not a member of the UN, but is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[49]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[50]</a></sup> both <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">specialized agencies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">United Nations System</a>. The Republic of Kosovo is <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">recognised by&#160;111&#160;UN member states</a>, including three of the five permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> (France, the United Kingdom, and the United States), while the other two—China and Russia—do not recognise Kosovo. On 22 July 2010, the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>, the primary judicial organ of the UN, issued an <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice_advisory_opinion_on_Kosovo%27s_declaration_of_independence" title="International Court of Justice advisory opinion on Kosovo's declaration of independence">advisory opinion</a>, ruling that Kosovo's declaration of independence was not in violation of international law.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Suspension.2C_expulsion.2C_and_withdrawal_of_members">Suspension, expulsion, and withdrawal of members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Suspension, expulsion, and withdrawal of members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_from_the_United_Nations" title="Withdrawal from the United Nations">Withdrawal from the United Nations</a></div>
<p>A member state may be suspended or expelled from the UN, according to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Charter" title="United Nations Charter">United Nations Charter</a>. From <a href="/wiki/Chapter_II_of_the_United_Nations_Charter" title="Chapter II of the United Nations Charter">Chapter II</a>, Article 5:<sup id="cite_ref-charter_ch2_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter_ch2-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>A Member of the United Nations against which preventive or enforcement action has been taken by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> may be suspended from the exercise of the rights and privileges of membership by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly</a> upon the recommendation of the Security Council. The exercise of these rights and privileges may be restored by the Security Council.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>From Article 6:<sup id="cite_ref-charter_ch2_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter_ch2-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>A Member of the United Nations which has persistently violated the Principles contained in the present Charter may be expelled from the Organization by the General Assembly upon the recommendation of the Security Council.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Since its inception, no member state has been suspended or expelled from the UN under Articles 5 and 6. However, in a few cases, states were suspended or expelled from participating in UN activities by means other than Articles 5 and 6:</p>
<ul>
<li>On 25 October 1971, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_2758" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758">United Nations General Assembly Resolution 2758</a> was adopted, which recognized the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> instead of the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> (since 1949 controlling only Taiwan) as the legitimate representative of China in the UN and effectively expelled the Republic of China from the UN in 1971 <i>(see the section <a href="#Republic_of_China">Former members: Republic of China</a>)</i>. This act did not constitute as the expulsion of a member state under Article 6, as this would have required Security Council approval and been subjected to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">vetoes</a> by its permanent members, which included the Republic of China itself and the United States, which at that time still recognized the Republic of China.<sup id="cite_ref-bolton_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bolton-80">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>In October 1974, the Security Council considered a draft resolution that would have recommended that the General Assembly immediately expel South Africa from the UN, in compliance with Article 6 of the United Nations Charter, due to <a href="/wiki/Apartheid_in_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Apartheid in South Africa">its apartheid policies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup> However, the resolution was not adopted because of vetoes by three permanent members of the Security Council: France, the United Kingdom, and the United States. In response, the General Assembly decided to suspend South Africa from participation in the work of the Assembly's 29th session on 12 November 1974; however, South Africa was not formally suspended under Article 5. The suspension lasted until the General Assembly welcomed South Africa back to full participation in the UN on 23 June 1994, following its successful democratic <a href="/wiki/South_African_general_election,_1994" title="South African general election, 1994">elections earlier that year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li>On 28 April 1992, the new <a href="/wiki/Serbia_and_Montenegro" title="Serbia and Montenegro">Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> was established, by the remaining republics of Serbia and Montenegro of the former <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>. On 22 September 1992, United Nations General Assembly Resolution A/RES/47/1 was adopted, by which it considered that "the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia (Serbia and Montenegro) cannot continue automatically the membership of the former Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia in the United Nations," and therefore decided that "the Federal Republic of Yugoslavia (Serbia and Montenegro) should apply for membership in the United Nations and that it shall not participate in the work of the General Assembly". It did not apply for membership until <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a> was ousted from the presidency and was admitted on 1 November 2000 <i>(see the section <a href="#Yugoslavia">Former members: Yugoslavia</a>)</i>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Withdrawal_of_Indonesia_.281965.E2.80.931966.29">Withdrawal of Indonesia (1965–1966)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Withdrawal of Indonesia (1965–1966)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/CONEFO" title="CONEFO">CONEFO</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soekarno.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A black-and-white three-quarters view of Sukarno's face" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Soekarno.jpg/170px-Soekarno.jpg" width="170" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c5/Soekarno.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="196" data-file-height="290" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soekarno.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Indonesian president <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>'s decision to withdraw from the United Nations in 1965 is the only instance of a withdrawal of membership in UN history. <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> rejoined the UN a year later.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the inception of the UN, only one member state (excluding those that dissolved or merged with other member states) has unilaterally withdrawn from the UN. During the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia%E2%80%93Malaysia_confrontation" title="Indonesia–Malaysia confrontation">Indonesia–Malaysia confrontation</a>, and in response to the election of <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="List of members of the United Nations Security Council">non-permanent member of the United Nations Security Council</a>, in a letter dated 20 January 1965, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> informed the <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">United Nations Secretary-General</a> that it had decided "at this stage and under the present circumstances" to withdraw from the UN. However, following the overthrow of <a href="/wiki/President_of_Indonesia" title="President of Indonesia">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">Sukarno</a>, in a telegram dated 19 September 1966, Indonesia notified the Secretary-General of its decision "to resume full cooperation with the United Nations and to resume participation in its activities starting with the twenty-first session of the General Assembly". On 28 September 1966, the United Nations General Assembly took note of the decision of the Government of Indonesia and the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="President of the United Nations General Assembly">President</a> invited the representatives of that country to take their seats in the Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-yearbook_64-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yearbook-64">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike suspension and expulsion, no express provision is made in the United Nations Charter of whether or how a member can legally withdraw from the UN (largely to prevent the threat of withdrawal from being used as a form of political blackmail, or to evade obligations under the Charter, similar to withdrawals that weakened the UN's predecessor, the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-bolton_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bolton-80">[52]</a></sup> or on whether a request for readmission by a withdrawn member should be treated the same as an application for membership, i.e., requiring Security Council as well as General Assembly approval. Indonesia's return to the UN would suggest that this is not required; however, scholars have argued that the course of action taken by the General Assembly was not in accordance with the Charter from a legal point of view.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Observers_and_non-members">Observers and non-members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Observers and non-members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">United Nations General Assembly observers</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Holy_See_and_the_United_Nations" title="Holy See and the United Nations">Holy See and the United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palestine_194" title="Palestine 194">Palestine 194</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Union_and_the_United_Nations" title="European Union and the United Nations">European Union and the United Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Flags_-_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Nations_Flags_-_cropped.jpg/220px-United_Nations_Flags_-_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Nations_Flags_-_cropped.jpg/330px-United_Nations_Flags_-_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/United_Nations_Flags_-_cropped.jpg/440px-United_Nations_Flags_-_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4384" data-file-height="2923" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Nations_Flags_-_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> has been neutral in international conflicts since the early 19th century and joined the UN as a full member only in 2002. Despite this, the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Nations" title="Palace of Nations">Palace of Nations</a> in Geneva has hosted the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Geneva" title="United Nations Office at Geneva">United Nations Office at Geneva</a> since 1946 and also previously served as the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to the member states, there are two <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers#Non-member_states" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">non-member permanent observer states</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> and the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gharib_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gharib-83">[55]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> holds sovereignty over the state of <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> and maintains diplomatic relations with 180 other states. It has been an observer state since 6 April 1964,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[56]</a></sup> and gained all the rights of full membership except voting on 1 July 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a> was granted observer status as a "non-member entity" on 22 November 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[58]</a></sup> Acknowledging the proclamation of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Council" title="Palestinian National Council">Palestine National Council</a> on 15 November 1988, the United Nations General Assembly decided that, effective as of 15 December 1988, the designation "Palestine" should be used in place of the designation "Palestine Liberation Organization" in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_System" title="United Nations System">United Nations System</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[59]</a></sup> On 23 September 2011, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority" title="Palestinian National Authority">Palestinian National Authority</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Palestinian_National_Authority" title="President of the Palestinian National Authority">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a> submitted the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_194" title="Palestine 194">application for UN membership</a> for the State of Palestine to <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">United Nations Secretary-General</a> <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[61]</a></sup> the application has not been voted on by the UN Security Council. On 31 October 2011, the General Assembly of <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> voted to admit Palestine as a member, becoming the first UN agency to admit Palestine as a full member.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[62]</a></sup> The State of Palestine was recognized as a "non-member state" on 29 November 2012, when the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_resolution_67/19" title="United Nations General Assembly resolution 67/19">United Nations General Assembly resolution 67/19</a> by a vote of 138 to 9, with 41 abstentions.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[65]</a></sup> The change in status was described by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> as "de facto recognition of the sovereign state of Palestine".<sup id="cite_ref-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNStatehoodBid2012accepted-94">[66]</a></sup> On 17 December 2012, UN Chief of Protocol Yeocheol Yoon decided that "the designation of 'State of Palestine' shall be used by the Secretariat in all official United Nations documents".<sup id="cite_ref-Gharib_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gharib-83">[55]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>A number of states were also granted observer status before being admitted to the UN as full members <i>(see <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers#Former_non-member_observer_states" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">United Nations General Assembly observers</a> for the full list)</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-osmanczyk_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osmanczyk-96">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[69]</a></sup> The most recent case of an observer state becoming a member state was <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, which was admitted in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> institution, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, was granted observer status at the UNGA through Resolution 3208 in 1974. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> in 2009 resulted in the delegates being accredited directly to the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[71]</a></sup> It was accorded full rights in the General Assembly, bar the right to vote and put forward candidates, via UNGA Resolution A/RES/65/276 on 10 May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[72]</a></sup> It is the only non-state party to over 50 multilateral conventions, and has participated as a full member in every way except for having a vote in a number of UN conferences.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The sovereignty status of <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> is in dispute between <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Polisario_Front" title="Polisario Front">Polisario Front</a>. Most of the territory is controlled by Morocco, the remainder (the <a href="/wiki/Free_Zone_(region)" title="Free Zone (region)">Free Zone</a>) by the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic</a>, proclaimed by the Polisario Front. Western Sahara is listed by the UN as a "<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">non-self-governing territory</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a>, which are both <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">associated states</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, are not members of the UN, but are members of <a href="/wiki/List_of_specialized_agencies_of_the_United_Nations" title="List of specialized agencies of the United Nations">specialized agencies of the UN</a> such as <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[75]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[76]</a></sup> and have had their "full treaty-making capacity" recognized by <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretariat" title="United Nations Secretariat">United Nations Secretariat</a> in 1992 and 1994 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-art102_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art102-105">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-map_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-map-106">[78]</a></sup> They have since become parties to a number of international treaties which the UN Secretariat acts as a <a href="/wiki/Depositary" title="Depositary">depositary</a> for, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[79]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_on_the_Law_of_the_Sea" title="United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea">United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[80]</a></sup> and are treated as non-member states.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[82]</a></sup> The Cook Islands has expressed a desire to become a UN member state, but New Zealand has said that they would not support the application without a change in their constitutional relationship, in particular the right of Cook Islanders to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_nationality_law" title="New Zealand nationality law">New Zealand citizenship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[83]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Benin: Name was changed from <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Dahomey" title="Republic of Dahomey">Dahomey</a> on 1 December 1975.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bolivia (Plurinational State of): Previously referred to as Bolivia.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Burkina Faso: Name was changed from <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Upper_Volta" title="Republic of Upper Volta">Upper Volta</a> on 6 August 1984.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cabo Verde: Previously referred to as Cape Verde. On 24 October 2013, Cabo Verde requested that its name no longer be translated into different languages.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cambodia: Name was changed to the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Republic" title="Khmer Republic">Khmer Republic</a> on 7 October 1970, and back to Cambodia on 30 April 1975. Name was changed again to <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Kampuchea" title="Democratic Kampuchea">Democratic Kampuchea</a> on 6 April 1976, and back to Cambodia on 3 February 1990.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Cameroon: Previously referred to as <a href="/wiki/Cameroun" class="mw-redirect" title="Cameroun">Cameroun</a> (before merging with <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cameroons" title="Southern Cameroons">Southern Cameroons</a> in 1961). By a letter of 4 January 1974, the Secretary-General was informed that Cameroon had changed its name to the United Republic of Cameroon. Name was changed back to Cameroon on 4 February 1984.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Central African Republic: By a letter of 20 December 1976, the Central African Republic advised that it had changed its name to the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Empire" title="Central African Empire">Central African Empire</a>. Name was changed back to the Central African Republic on 20 September 1979.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Congo: Previously referred to as Congo (Brazzaville) (to differentiate it from Congo (Leopoldville)) and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="People's Republic of the Congo">People's Republic of the Congo</a>. Name was changed to Congo on 15 November 1971 (after the Democratic Republic of the Congo changed its name to Zaire). Also referred to as Congo (Republic of the).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-25">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Côte d'Ivoire: Previously referred to as Ivory Coast. On 6 November 1985, Côte d'Ivoire requested that its name no longer be translated into different languages; this became fully effective on 1 January 1986.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Democratic Republic of the Congo: Previously referred to as <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo_(L%C3%A9opoldville)" title="Republic of the Congo (Léopoldville)">Congo (Leopoldville)</a> (to differentiate it from Congo (Brazzaville)). Name was changed from the Democratic Republic of the Congo to <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> on 27 October 1971, and back to the Democratic Republic of the Congo on 17 May 1997.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Gambia: Previously referred to as The Gambia.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Withdrew from the UN on 20 January 1965. It rejoined on 28 September 1966.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-29">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Iran (Islamic Republic of): Previously referred to as Iran. By a communication of 5 March 1981, Iran informed the Secretary-General that it should be referred to by its complete name of the Islamic Republic of Iran.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Kazakhstan: Spelling was changed from Kazakstan on 20 June 1997.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lao People's Democratic Republic: Name was changed from Laos on 2 December 1975.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Libya: Formerly recognised as the Libyan Arab Republic from 1969 after originally being admitted as Libya. By <i>notes verbales</i> of 1 and 21 April 1977, the Libyan Arab Republic advised that it had changed its name to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Libya_under_Muammar_Gaddafi#Great_Socialist_People.27s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya_.281977.E2.80.932011.29" title="History of Libya under Muammar Gaddafi">Libyan Arab Jamahiriya</a>. On 16 September 2011, the UN General Assembly awarded the UN seat to the <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">National Transitional Council</a>, thereby restoring the original name of Libya.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Madagascar: Previously referred to as the Malagasy Republic.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Maldives: Previously referred to as the Maldive Islands.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Myanmar: Name was changed from Burma on 18 June 1989.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Philippines: Previously referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_the_Philippines" title="Commonwealth of the Philippines">Philippine Commonwealth</a> (before becoming a republic in 1946) and as the Philippine Republic.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Republic of Moldova: Previously referred to as Moldova.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Saint Kitts and Nevis: Name was changed officially from Saint Christopher and Nevis on 26 November 1986; the UN, however, continued to use the former name throughout the year.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sao Tome and Principe: The official UN designation lacks <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a>; however, the name is constitutionally defined as São Tomé and Príncipe, with diacritics.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">South Africa: Previously referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> (before becoming a republic in 1961).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sri Lanka: Name was changed from <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon" title="Dominion of Ceylon">Ceylon</a> on 22 May 1972.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Suriname: Name was changed from Surinam on 23 January 1978.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Thailand: Previously referred to as Siam.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Venezuela (Bolivarian Republic of): Previously referred to as Venezuela.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Member_states_of_the_United_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/Depts/Cartographic/map/profile/world.pdf">"The World"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. United Nations.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMember+states+of+the+United+Nations&amp;rft.btitle=The+World&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.un.org%2FDepts%2FCartographic%2Fmap%2Fprofile%2Fworld.pdf&amp;rft.pub=United+Nations&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span> The following territories are excluded as the UN does not consider them as part of any member state: <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> is a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers#Non-member_states" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">UN non-member observer state</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a> (<a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a> is a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers#Non-member_states" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">UN non-member observer state</a>), <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> (status in dispute between <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Polisario_Front" title="Polisario Front">Polisario Front</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> (regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System" title="Antarctic Treaty System">Antarctic Treaty System</a>). Territories of <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">states not recognized by the UN</a> are not excluded due to the UN's position that they are part of some UN member state, including, for example, the territories governed by the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Republic of China</a> (<a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="List of islands of the Republic of China">other smaller islands</a>), as the UN members voted to consider the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a> as the only lawful representative of <a href="/wiki/China_and_the_United_Nations" title="China and the United Nations">China at the UN</a> and the UN chooses not to question <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan#Position_of_the_People.27s_Republic_of_China_.28PRC.29" title="Political status of Taiwan">its claim that Taiwan is part of China</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/depts/dhl/unms/whatisms.shtml">"What are Member States?"</a>. United Nations.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMember+states+of+the+United+Nations&amp;rft.btitle=What+are+Member+States%3F&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.un.org%2Fdepts%2Fdhl%2Funms%2Fwhatisms.shtml&amp;rft.pub=United+Nations&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Toeplar, Stefan (2009). <i>International Encyclopedia of Civil Society</i>. p.&#160;114.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMember+states+of+the+United+Nations&amp;rft.aufirst=Stefan&amp;rft.aulast=Toeplar&amp;rft.btitle=International+Encyclopedia+of+Civil+Society&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.pages=114&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-charter_ch2-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-charter_ch2_4-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-charter_ch2_4-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-charter_ch2_4-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/en/documents/charter/chapter2.shtml">"Charter of the United Nations, Chapter II: Membership"</a>. United Nations.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMember+states+of+the+United+Nations&amp;rft.btitle=Charter+of+the+United+Nations%2C+Chapter+II%3A+Membership&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.un.org%2Fen%2Fdocuments%2Fcharter%2Fchapter2.shtml&amp;rft.pub=United+Nations&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/en/members/about.shtml">"About UN Membership"</a>. United Nations.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMember+states+of+the+United+Nations&amp;rft.btitle=About+UN+Membership&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.un.org%2Fen%2Fmembers%2Fabout.shtml&amp;rft.pub=United+Nations&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

United Nations.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMember+states+of+the+United+Nations&amp;rft.btitle=Growth+in+United+Nations+membership%2C+1945%93present&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.un.org%2Fen%2Fmembers%2Fgrowth.shtml&amp;rft.pub=United+Nations&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/aboutun/unhistory/">"History of the United Nations"</a>.
